<p><b>Raheem Shaquille Sterling</b> (born 8 December 1994) is an English professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Winger" title="Forward (association football)">winger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">attacking midfielder</a> for <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> and the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national team</a>.
</p><p>Born in Jamaica, Sterling moved to London at the age of five and began his career at <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> before signing for <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> in 2010. He was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Boy_(award)" title="Golden Boy (award)">Golden Boy</a> award in 2014. In July 2015, following a lengthy dispute over a new contract, he was signed by Manchester City in a transfer potentially worth £49&#160;million, the highest transfer fee ever paid for an English player at the time. He then went on to help Manchester City win back-to-back Premier League titles in the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Premier_League" title="2017–18 Premier League">2017–18</a> and <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Premier_League" title="2018–19 Premier League">2018–19</a> seasons. In the 2018–19 season, he was named to the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Premier League Team of the Year</a> and won the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Young_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Young Player of the Year">PFA Young Player of the Year</a> and <a href="/wiki/FWA_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="FWA Footballer of the Year">FWA Footballer of the Year</a>.
</p><p>Sterling made his senior debut for England in November 2012 after previously being <a href="/wiki/Cap_(sport)" title="Cap (sport)">capped</a> by <a href="/wiki/England_national_youth_football_team" title="England national youth football team">England youth teams</a> at <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-16_football_team" title="England national under-16 football team">under-16</a>, <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-17_football_team" title="England national under-17 football team">under-17</a>, <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-19_football_team" title="England national under-19 football team">under-19</a> and <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-21_football_team" title="England national under-21 football team">under-21</a> levels. He was chosen in <a href="/wiki/List_of_England_national_football_team_World_Cup_and_European_Championship_squads" title="List of England national football team World Cup and European Championship squads">England's squads</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014</a> and <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cups</a> and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Sterling was born in the Maverley district of <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">Kingston</a>, Jamaica, and spent his early years there.<sup id="cite_ref-gleaner-2011-02-23_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gleaner-2011-02-23-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gleaner-2012-07-01_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gleaner-2012-07-01-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> His mother, Nadine Clarke, was previously a competitive athlete in the Jamaican national athletics team; Sterling credits her for his unique running style.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> His absent father was murdered in Jamaica when Sterling was two years old.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> At the age of five, he emigrated to Neasden, London with his mother,<sup id="cite_ref-gleaner-2011-02-23_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gleaner-2011-02-23-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gleaner-2012-07-01_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gleaner-2012-07-01-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and attended <a href="/wiki/Copland_Community_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Copland Community School">Copland School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wembley" title="Wembley">Wembley</a>, North West London.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Due to behavioural problems, Sterling spent three years at Vernon House, a specialist school in Neasden.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span></h3>
<p>Sterling spent four years with local youth team Alpha &amp; Omega before signing for <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a>, at age 10, as a winger. Sterling was subsequently scouted by the Academies of <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C._Under-23s_and_Academy" title="Arsenal F.C. Under-23s and Academy">Arsenal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C._Under-23s_and_Academy" title="Chelsea F.C. Under-23s and Academy">Chelsea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C._Academy" title="Fulham F.C. Academy">Fulham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C._Reserves_and_Academy" title="Liverpool F.C. Reserves and Academy">Liverpool</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C._EDS_and_Academy" title="Manchester City F.C. EDS and Academy">Manchester City</a>. However, he was encouraged by his mother not to choose clubs in the locality in order to escape the hostile gang culture in London.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liverpool">Liverpool</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Raheem_Sterling_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Raheem_Sterling_2011.jpg/170px-Raheem_Sterling_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Raheem_Sterling_2011.jpg/255px-Raheem_Sterling_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Raheem_Sterling_2011.jpg/340px-Raheem_Sterling_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="1675" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Raheem_Sterling_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sterling warming up for <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> in 2011</div></div></div>
<p>Sterling was signed by <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> from the academy at <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> in February 2010 by then academy director Frank McParland, and <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez" title="Rafael Benítez">Rafael Benítez</a>, for an initial fee of £450,000, with the possibility of rising up to £2&#160;million depending on how many appearances he made for the first team.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He initially played in the club's <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C._Reserves_and_Academy" title="Liverpool F.C. Reserves and Academy">youth team</a>, making his debut in an Under-18s derby match against Everton.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Sterling scored his first goal for Liverpool in a friendly match against <a href="/wiki/Hibernian_F.C." title="Hibernian F.C.">Hibernian</a>, which ended in a 2–2 draw. His first <a href="/wiki/Premier_Academy_League" title="Premier Academy League">Premier Academy League</a> match was a 2–2 draw against <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C._Reserves_and_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Aston Villa F.C. Reserves and Academy">Aston Villa</a>, with his first win coming at home to <a href="/wiki/Bristol_City_F.C." title="Bristol City F.C.">Bristol City</a> a week later. On 15 December, he scored in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Youth_Cup" title="FA Youth Cup">FA Youth Cup</a> in a 4–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Notts_County_F.C." title="Notts County F.C.">Notts County</a>. On 14 February 2011, Sterling scored five goals in a 9–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Southend_United_F.C." title="Southend United F.C.">Southend United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 March 2012, Sterling made his senior Liverpool debut as a <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)" title="Substitute (association football)">substitute</a> in a league match against <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a>, aged 17 years and 107 days, becoming the third-youngest player to play for the club.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> He made two more appearances over the remainder of the campaign, again as a substitute.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2012.E2.80.9314:_Development_and_breakthrough"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–14:_Development_and_breakthrough">2012–14: Development and breakthrough</span></h4>
<p>In August 2012, he made his European debut for the club, coming on as a substitute in a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> qualifying match against <a href="/wiki/FC_Gomel" title="FC Gomel">Gomel</a>, replacing <a href="/wiki/Joe_Cole" title="Joe Cole">Joe Cole</a> in a 0–1 away win.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The following week, Sterling scored his first goal for the senior team with a first-half strike in a friendly against <a href="/wiki/Bayer_04_Leverkusen" title="Bayer 04 Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a>. On 23 August 2012, he started his first match for Liverpool in a Europa League qualifying match away to <a href="/wiki/Heart_of_Midlothian_F.C." title="Heart of Midlothian F.C.">Hearts</a> in a 0–1 win.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He was given his first start in the league three days later in a 2–2 draw at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a> to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He played the full 90 minutes in the loss to <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> on 2 September, and the draw with <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a> on 15 September, where he registered one assist and was named man of the match. On 19 September, Sterling was one of the group of teenagers that travelled to Switzerland to play <a href="/wiki/BSC_Young_Boys" title="BSC Young Boys">Young Boys</a> in a UEFA Europa League group match. He replaced <a href="/wiki/Stewart_Downing" title="Stewart Downing">Stewart Downing</a> in the second half as Liverpool won 3–5.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> On 20 October, Sterling scored his first senior competitive goal for Liverpool in the 29th minute of a 1–0 league win against <a href="/wiki/Reading_F.C." title="Reading F.C.">Reading</a> with a strike from the edge of the box. As a result, he became the second-youngest player to score in a competitive fixture for Liverpool, behind only <a href="/wiki/Michael_Owen" title="Michael Owen">Michael Owen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 December 2012, Sterling signed a contract extension, committing his future to Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> He scored his second league goal for the club on 2 January 2013, opening the scoring in a 3–0 win against Sunderland with a lob over goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Simon_Mignolet" title="Simon Mignolet">Simon Mignolet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Raheem_Sterling_v_PNE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Raheem_Sterling_v_PNE.jpg/170px-Raheem_Sterling_v_PNE.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Raheem_Sterling_v_PNE.jpg/255px-Raheem_Sterling_v_PNE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Raheem_Sterling_v_PNE.jpg/340px-Raheem_Sterling_v_PNE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2716" data-file-height="3084" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Raheem_Sterling_v_PNE.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sterling playing for Liverpool in 2013</div></div></div>
<p>On 27 August 2013, Sterling scored his first goal of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2013–14 Liverpool F.C. season">2013–14 season</a>, the opening goal against Notts County in a 4–2 win in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Football_League_Cup" title="2013–14 Football League Cup">League Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> On 4 December, Sterling scored his first Premier League goal of the season for Liverpool in a 5–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a>. His form in December saw him score two further goals in wins against <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> (5–0) and <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> (3–1).<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> On 8 February 2014, he scored twice in a 5–1 win against Arsenal at Anfield.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> On 13 April, he scored Liverpool's opening goal in a 3–2 win over Manchester City.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> A week later, he scored two goals and assisted another as Liverpool won 2–3 against Norwich City at <a href="/wiki/Carrow_Road" title="Carrow Road">Carrow Road</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 18 April 2014, Sterling was named as one of the six players on the shortlist for the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Young_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Young Player of the Year">PFA Young Player of the Year</a> award.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> He was named Liverpool Chartered Player of the Month for April.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> At the end of the season, he was named Liverpool's Young Player of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2014.E2.80.9315:_Final_season_with_Liverpool"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–15:_Final_season_with_Liverpool">2014–15: Final season with Liverpool</span></h4>
<p>On 17 August 2014, Sterling scored to help Liverpool to win their opening match of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2014–15 Liverpool F.C. season">2014–15 season</a>, a 2–1 win at home to <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> at Anfield.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> On 31 August, Sterling scored the opening goal in a 0–3 league win against Tottenham at <a href="/wiki/White_Hart_Lane" title="White Hart Lane">White Hart Lane</a> and was named man of the match.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Sterling was named the Liverpool Player of the Month for August.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 16 September, Sterling made his <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> debut in a 2–1 victory over Bulgarian champions <a href="/wiki/PFC_Ludogorets_Razgrad" title="PFC Ludogorets Razgrad">Ludogorets Razgrad</a> at Anfield.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On 14 December 2014, he made his 100th appearance for Liverpool in a match against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On 17 December, Sterling scored a brace in a 1–3 victory over <a href="/wiki/A.F.C._Bournemouth" class="mw-redirect" title="A.F.C. Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a> at <a href="/wiki/Dean_Court" title="Dean Court">Dean Court</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Football_League_Cup" title="2014–15 Football League Cup">League Cup</a> quarter-final.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 December, Sterling was named as the recipient of the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Golden_Boy_(award)" title="Golden Boy (award)">Golden Boy award</a>. "It's down to hard work. I'm really happy that people are recognising that I'm trying to work hard and do my best for this football club. I'm really grateful for this award," he stated upon receiving the award.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Liverpool_Echo_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liverpool_Echo-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Sterling was officially excused from Liverpool's FA Cup match against <a href="/wiki/AFC_Wimbledon" title="AFC Wimbledon">AFC Wimbledon</a> in January 2015, with manager <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Rodgers" title="Brendan Rodgers">Brendan Rodgers</a> aiming to prevent the player becoming exhausted. He used the time off to holiday in Jamaica.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Willian_Sterling_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Willian_Sterling_2015.jpg/170px-Willian_Sterling_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Willian_Sterling_2015.jpg/255px-Willian_Sterling_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Willian_Sterling_2015.jpg/340px-Willian_Sterling_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2027" data-file-height="3041" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Willian_Sterling_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sterling (right) playing for Liverpool in 2015</div></div></div>
<p>On 20 January 2015, Sterling scored a fine solo goal against <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> in a 1–1 draw in the League Cup semi-final first leg at Anfield, going past <a href="/wiki/Nemanja_Mati%C4%87" title="Nemanja Mati">Nemanja Mati</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gary_Cahill" title="Gary Cahill">Gary Cahill</a> before beating <a href="/wiki/Thibaut_Courtois" title="Thibaut Courtois">Thibaut Courtois</a> to find the net.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On 31 January, Sterling scored the opening goal in a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> On 4 February, Sterling scored the equaliser against <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Macron_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Macron Stadium">Macron Stadium</a> in a 1–2 away win for Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> On 22 February, he scored the second goal for Liverpool in a 0–2 win over Southampton.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 13 April, Sterling opened the scoring in a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> He was named the team's Young Player of the Season on 19 May for the second consecutive year in a row, and when receiving the award was booed by fans due to his rejection of a new contract;<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> he was also booed on 7 June, while playing for England in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> On 16 April 2015, for the second consecutive year, he was named as one of the six players on the shortlist for the PFA Young Player of the Year award.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Contract_dispute">Contract dispute</span></h4>
<p>On 9 February 2015, Brendan Rodgers said that Sterling had been offered "an incredible deal" to stay at Liverpool, rumoured to be a new contract worth £100,000 a week, but he also stated Liverpool were "certainly not a club that is going to give way, way above what a player is worth at a certain time in their career."<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> However, on 20 March, Rodgers said Sterling's contract situation would not be resolved until the summer at least.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 April, Sterling gave an unsanctioned interview with the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>, where he confirmed he had turned down a new deal, but denied that this was for reasons of money. He had two years of a £35,000 per week contract remaining and said that he would not negotiate a new contract until the end of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Four days later, Brendan Rodgers criticised Sterling's advisors (Aidy Ward) for the interview, saying, "You are not a 20-year-old boy and you pick up the phone and ask to speak to the BBC. You don't do it. Him in particular. But, of course, if he is asked to do that by other parties then that is what he'll do."<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 May, amid rumours that Sterling intended to leave the club his agent, Ward gave an interview to the <i><a href="/wiki/London_Evening_Standard" class="mw-redirect" title="London Evening Standard">London Evening Standard</a></i> saying, "I don't care about the PR of the club and the club situation... He is definitely not signing. He's not signing for £700, £800, £900 thousand a week."<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 June, Liverpool reportedly rejected an initial bid of £30&#160;million from Manchester City. One week later, they reportedly rejected a second bid from City for £40&#160;million, with Liverpool valuing Sterling at £50&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Sterling reportedly later asked to be left out of Liverpool's preseason tour to Asia, and missed two days of training through illness, which was met with widespread criticism from former Liverpool players, including <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Carragher" title="Jamie Carragher">Jamie Carragher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Souness" title="Graeme Souness">Graeme Souness</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_City">Manchester City</span></h3>
<h4><span id="2015.E2.80.9316:_Record_breaking_transfer_and_debut_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–16:_Record_breaking_transfer_and_debut_season">2015–16: Record breaking transfer and debut season</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Raheem_Sterling_(24366304179)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Raheem_Sterling_%2824366304179%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Raheem_Sterling_%2824366304179%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="298" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Raheem_Sterling_%2824366304179%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Raheem_Sterling_%2824366304179%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Raheem_Sterling_%2824366304179%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Raheem_Sterling_%2824366304179%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1518" data-file-height="2659" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Raheem_Sterling_(24366304179)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sterling playing for <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> in 2016</div></div></div>
<p>On 12 July 2015, a deal was agreed for his transfer to Manchester City for an initial £44&#160;million, with a further potential £5&#160;million in add-ons, subject to personal terms and a medical, which would make him <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_association_football_transfers" title="List of most expensive association football transfers">the most expensive English player of all time</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> On 14 July, Sterling officially joined Manchester City, signing a five-year contract.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> His debut came on 10 August, starting as City began the season with a 0–3 win away to <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Nineteen days later, Sterling scored his first competitive goal for Manchester City in a 2–0 defeat of <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a> at the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Manchester_Stadium" title="City of Manchester Stadium">City of Manchester Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Sterling scored his first career <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> as City beat Bournemouth 5–1 on 17 October.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 3 November, Sterling scored his first UEFA Champions League goal in a 1–3 win away to <a href="/wiki/Sevilla_FC" title="Sevilla FC">Sevilla</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> On 8 December, he scored twice in the final ten minutes of City's last <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage" title="2015–16 UEFA Champions League group stage">group stage</a> fixture against <a href="/wiki/Borussia_M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Borussia Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</a>, helping turn a 1–2 deficit into a 4–2 win and ensuring City overtook <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> in the final group standings.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> On 20 March 2016, he suffered a <a href="/wiki/Strain_(injury)" title="Strain (injury)">groin injury</a> in a 1–0 loss to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_derby" title="Manchester derby">rivals</a> Manchester United, and was ruled out for 8 weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Sterling eventually lost his place in the starting line-up.<sup id="cite_ref-Manuel_Pellegrini_explains_why_Raheem_Sterling_has_been_dropped_to_the_bench_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manuel_Pellegrini_explains_why_Raheem_Sterling_has_been_dropped_to_the_bench-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2016.E2.80.9318:_Collective_and_individual_success"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016–18:_Collective_and_individual_success">2016–18: Collective and individual success</span></h4>
<p>Sterling appeared regularly for Manchester City under <a href="/wiki/Pep_Guardiola" title="Pep Guardiola">Pep Guardiola</a> for the opening matches of the 2016–17 season.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> He was <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Player of the Month">Premier League Player of the Month</a> for August 2016 after he scored two goals and provided one assist in three games.<sup id="cite_ref-premierleague.com_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-premierleague.com-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> On 21 February 2017, Sterling scored the opener before setting up a goal for <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Ag%C3%BCero" title="Sergio Agüero">Sergio Agüero</a> in a 5–3 home win against <a href="/wiki/AS_Monaco_FC" title="AS Monaco FC">Monaco</a> in the Champions League.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 26 August 2017, Sterling scored the winner in a 2–1 away win away to <a href="/wiki/AFC_Bournemouth" title="AFC Bournemouth">AFC Bournemouth</a> in stoppage time. He was sent off by <a href="/wiki/Mike_Dean_(referee)" title="Mike Dean (referee)">Mike Dean</a> with a second yellow after he celebrated among travelling supporters that had run onto the pitch.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> On 29 November 2017, Sterling scored a 96th-minute winner against Southampton in a 2–1 home win.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> He scored his eighteenth and final league goal of the season during a 5–0 victory at Swansea City on 22 April 2018, his most ever at this point in his career.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2018.E2.80.9319:_Domestic_treble_with_City"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–19:_Domestic_treble_with_City">2018–19: Domestic treble with City</span></h4>
<p>Following England's <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">World Cup campaign</a>, Sterling made an immediate return to the Manchester City starting line-up. On 12 August 2018, less than a month after starting in England's 2–0 loss against <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a> in the third place play-off, Sterling scored the opening goal in Manchester City's 2–0 away win against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The strike was Sterling's 50th Premier League goal.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> On 4 November 2018, Sterling scored twice and made two assists in a 6–1 win against Southampton at home, scoring his 50th goal for Manchester City in all competitions in the process.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In November 2018, he signed a three-year extension to keep him at City until 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2018, Sterling alleged that sections of the media served to "fuel racism" with their portrayal of young black footballers. The comments emerged after Sterling was subjected to alleged racist abuse during City's 2–0 defeat at Chelsea.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He began 2019 with a 2–1 win against Liverpool, where he assisted <a href="/wiki/Leroy_San%C3%A9" title="Leroy Sané">Leroy Sané</a>'s winning goal.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> On 6 January 2019, he scored a goal and assisted one in a 7–0 win against Rotherham, which booked their place in the fourth round.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> On 20 January 2019, he headed a goal to help City win 3–0 over Huddersfield Town.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> On 3 February 2019, he helped assist two of <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Ag%C3%BCero" title="Sergio Agüero">Sergio Agüero</a>'s goal to beat Arsenal 3–1, which helped City move 2 points behind Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> On 10 February 2019, he scored two goals to beat Chelsea 6–0 at the Etihad.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> On 20 February 2019, in a first leg match of the Champions League against <a href="/wiki/FC_Schalke_04" title="FC Schalke 04">Schalke</a>, he scored the winning goal in the 90th minute in a 3–2 win.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> In the EFL Cup Final on 24 February 2019, he scored the winning penalty in the penalty shootout to win the cup.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The following month, he scored a hat-trick for the first time since 2015 within the space of 13 minutes – the fastest hat-trick of the season – to secure a 3–1 victory over <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> He scored again in the return leg of Man City's Champions League clash with Schalke to help the club record a 7–0 (10–2) victory and equal the record for the largest winning margin in the knockout-phase of the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> On 17 April 2019, Sterling scored two and had a winner on aggregate disallowed in injury time - which would've sealed his third hat-trick in the season - in Manchester City's 4–3 win over Tottenham Hotspur in their UEFA Champions League quarter-final second-leg, however they were knocked out on away goals after losing 1–0 in the first leg.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> On 18 May 2019, Sterling scored twice as Manchester City defeated Watford 6–0 in the <a href="/wiki/2019_FA_Cup_Final" title="2019 FA Cup Final">2019 FA Cup Final</a> to clinch a domestic treble.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 2018–19 season, he was named to the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Premier League Team of the Year</a> and won the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Young_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Young Player of the Year">PFA Young Player of the Year</a> and <a href="/wiki/FWA_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="FWA Footballer of the Year">FWA Footballer of the Year</a>.
</p>
<h4><span id="2019.E2.80.9320_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2019–20_season">2019–20 season</span></h4>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2019_FA_Community_Shield" title="2019 FA Community Shield">2019 FA Community Shield</a> against Liverpool on 4 August, Sterling scored the opening goal of the match in an eventual 1–1 draw; Manchester City ultimately won the title 5–4 on penalties.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In Manchester City's opening game of the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Premier_League" title="2019–20 Premier League">2019–20 Premier League</a>, Sterling scored a second-half hat-trick – his third of the calendar year – in a 5–0 away win over West Ham, which put them top of the table on goal difference after one game.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> On 22 October 2019, Sterling scored his first UEFA Champions League hat-trick in a 5–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Atalanta_B.C." title="Atalanta B.C.">Atalanta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2020, during an interview with AS, Sterling was asked whether he would one day like to play for <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF" title="Real Madrid CF">Real Madrid</a>. In reply, Sterling explained that "No one knows what the future will hold. I am a player and I am always open to challenges but right now my challenge is at City and I'm really happy".<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 July 2020, Sterling scored his third hat-trick of the season in a 5–0 away thrashing of <a href="/wiki/Brighton_%26_Hove_Albion_F.C." title="Brighton &amp; Hove Albion F.C.">Brighton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> He scored another three goals in the last three league games of the season, ending with a total of 20 goals, his best ever tally in the Premier League.
</p><p>On 7 August 2020, he scored the opening goal in a 2–1 home victory against Real Madrid, knocking them out of the Champions League in the Round of 16. It was his 100th goal for City in all competitions, becoming the first Englishman to reach this figure for the club since <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Tueart" title="Dennis Tueart">Dennis Tueart</a> in 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2020.E2.80.9321_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2020–21_season">2020–21 season</span></h4>
<p>On 7 February 2021, Sterling scored a goal in a 4–1 away win over his former team Liverpool, to reach his 100th goal with Manchester City under Pep Guardiola in all competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth_teams">Youth teams</span></h3>
<p>Sterling's international career coincided with the introduction of the "<a href="/wiki/Home_Nations%27_gentlemen%27s_agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Home Nations&#39; gentlemen&#39;s agreement">home nations agreement</a>." It was not until September 2009 that <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> agreed to the proposals by the English, Northern Irish, Scottish and Welsh Football Associations to update the agreement, allowing players who were educated in their nation for five years or more to become eligible for their national team.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Sterling first represented England at under-16 level in November 2009 in a match against Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> When speaking of the possibility of playing for Jamaica, Sterling said, "When it comes to that decision, that is when I will decide, but if Jamaica calls for me, why not?"<sup id="cite_ref-gleaner-2009-11-11_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gleaner-2009-11-11-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sterling was selected to play for <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-17_football_team" title="England national under-17 football team">England</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_U-17_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA U-17 World Cup">2011 U-17 World Cup</a>. He scored a long-range goal in England's opening 2–0 win against <a href="/wiki/Rwanda_national_under-17_football_team" title="Rwanda national under-17 football team">Rwanda</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pachuca" title="Pachuca">Pachuca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> He also scored against <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_under-17_football_team" title="Argentina national under-17 football team">Argentina</a> in the second round in a match where England won 4–2 on penalties.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> On 10 September 2012, Sterling was called up to the senior <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> squad for the first time for a <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_H" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Group H">2014 World Cup qualifying</a> match against <a href="/wiki/Ukraine_national_football_team" title="Ukraine national football team">Ukraine</a>, where he was an unused substitute.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> In early October he was called up for the first time to the <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-21_football_team" title="England national under-21 football team">England under-21</a> squad and made his debut as a substitute during a match against Serbia on 16 October.<sup id="cite_ref-u21callup_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-u21callup-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-u21debut_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-u21debut-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal for England U21 on 13 August 2013, in a 6–0 win against <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_under-21_football_team" title="Scotland national under-21 football team">Scotland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Senior_team">Senior team</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Raheem_Sterling_2018-07-14_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Raheem_Sterling_2018-07-14_1.jpg/170px-Raheem_Sterling_2018-07-14_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Raheem_Sterling_2018-07-14_1.jpg/255px-Raheem_Sterling_2018-07-14_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Raheem_Sterling_2018-07-14_1.jpg/340px-Raheem_Sterling_2018-07-14_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="483" data-file-height="652" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Raheem_Sterling_2018-07-14_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sterling playing for <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a></div></div></div>
<p>Sterling made his senior debut for England on 14 November 2012, starting in a friendly away to <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> On 5 March 2014, Sterling earned his second cap and was named <a href="/wiki/Man_of_the_match" class="mw-redirect" title="Man of the match">man of the match</a> as England beat <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a> 1–0 in a friendly match at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 12 May 2014, Sterling was named in England's 23-man squad for the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> In a pre-tournament friendly on 4 June, against <a href="/wiki/Ecuador_national_football_team" title="Ecuador national football team">Ecuador</a> in Miami on his fourth cap, Sterling slid into <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Valencia" title="Antonio Valencia">Antonio Valencia</a>, who reacted by grabbing Sterling's neck; both received red cards for their actions.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Valencia later apologised for his reaction.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> On 14 June, Sterling started in England's opening group match, a 2–1 loss to <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manaus" title="Manaus">Manaus</a>, and was rated as the team's best performing player by the BBC.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 March 2015, Sterling scored his first senior goal for England in a 4–0 <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying">UEFA Euro 2016 qualifier</a> against <a href="/wiki/Lithuania_national_football_team" title="Lithuania national football team">Lithuania</a> at Wembley Stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-England_4–0_Lithuania_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-England_4–0_Lithuania-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> On 9 October 2015, Sterling scored his second goal of the qualifying campaign in a 2–0 victory against <a href="/wiki/Estonia_national_football_team" title="Estonia national football team">Estonia</a>, by which point the team were already qualified.<sup id="cite_ref-England_2–0_Estonia_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-England_2–0_Estonia-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> He was one of 23 players chosen for the final tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He was named in the 23-man <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national team</a> squad for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After a run of 27 games without a goal for England, Sterling scored twice in a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Nations_League" title="UEFA Nations League">UEFA Nations League</a> group game against <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a> on 15 October 2018. England went on to win the match 3–2.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sterling scored his first hat-trick for England on 22 March 2019 in a 5–0 win over the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic_national_football_team" title="Czech Republic national football team">Czech Republic</a> at Wembley Stadium in a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2020 qualifying">UEFA Euro 2020 qualifier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Czech_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Czech-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2019, Sterling scored a brace in a 6-0 defeat of <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_National_Football_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgaria National Football Team">Bulgaria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Sterling's first goal in the game meant that he equalled a record held jointly by <a href="/wiki/Eric_Brook" title="Eric Brook">Eric Brook</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francis_Lee_(footballer)" title="Francis Lee (footballer)">Francis Lee</a> of the most England goals scored by a Manchester City player (10). Sterling's second goal in the game meant that he became the sole record holder in this respect (although his second goal in the game was his twelfth England goal overall, it was his eleventh as a <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> player). 
</p><p>In November 2019 Sterling was dropped from the England team after clashing with international teammate but club rival <a href="/wiki/Joe_Gomez_(footballer)" title="Joe Gomez (footballer)">Joe Gomez</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span></h2>
<p>Sterling plays as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Winger" title="Forward (association football)">winger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">attacking midfielder</a> or <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Striker" title="Forward (association football)">striker</a>, though he is more comfortable as a natural winger.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Sterling has been praised for his adaptability and ability to play wide, at the tip of a midfield diamond and centrally, offering flexibility.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Known for his pace, low centre of gravity, and <a href="/wiki/Dribbling#Association_football" title="Dribbling">dribbling</a> skills,<sup id="cite_ref-Sterling_can_be_as_good_as_Marc_Overmars_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sterling_can_be_as_good_as_Marc_Overmars-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Sterling has been compared to <a href="/wiki/Alexis_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Alexis Sánchez">Alexis Sánchez</a> by his former manager Brendan Rodgers.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Rodgers has also praised him for offering a "real threat," his use of pace with composure and his maturity.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Despite his small stature, he also possesses considerable upper-body strength, which aids him in withstanding challenges, and retaining possession.<sup id="cite_ref-Sterling_can_be_as_good_as_Marc_Overmars_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sterling_can_be_as_good_as_Marc_Overmars-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Former <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> midfielder <a href="/wiki/Xavi" title="Xavi">Xavi</a> said in November 2014 that Sterling is good enough to play for the <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> club, praising his physical and technical qualities.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In April 2015, <i><a href="/wiki/BBC_Sport" title="BBC Sport">BBC Sport</a></i> columnist Phil McNulty wrote that Sterling was "very good with the potential to be outstanding" but remained a "work in progress" due to inconsistent performances. He also wrote, "He is blessed with natural pace that makes even the best defences and defenders take a step back."<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>In 2013, citing the influence of his mother, Sterling was quoted as saying he was "not 100 per cent religious but my belief is strong. When the time is right, I will fully be Christian."  He added that he put his faith in God and that he prays regularly.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> He has one daughter, Melody Rose, born in 2012 after a brief relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> His middle-name Shaquille comes from his grandmother, who was living in America at the time and wanted to name him after <a href="/wiki/Shaquille_O%27Neal" title="Shaquille O&#39;Neal">Shaquille O'Neal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 8 August 2013, Sterling was arrested for an alleged common assault on his former girlfriend, a model. He was found not guilty at Liverpool Magistrates Court on 20 September, when the complainant was unable to offer consistent evidence.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> A few months earlier, on 20 May 2013, a charge of common assault on a different woman was dropped after a witness failed to turn up to court.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2015, Sterling was photographed by the <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Mirror" title="Sunday Mirror">Sunday Mirror</a></i> allegedly smoking a <a href="/wiki/Hookah" title="Hookah">shisha pipe</a>, and by <a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)"><i>The Sun</i></a> allegedly inhaling <a href="/wiki/Nitrous_oxide" title="Nitrous oxide">nitrous oxide</a> for recreational purposes. Manager Brendan Rodgers said, "I don't think it is something you should be doing, it's as simple as that...Young players make mistakes. As long as they learn from them, that is what is important."<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2017, following the <a href="/wiki/Grenfell_Tower_fire" title="Grenfell Tower fire">Grenfell Tower fire</a> in which 71 people died, Sterling made a "substantial" donation to those affected by the fire.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 16 December 2017, Sterling was attacked outside Manchester City's training ground by a man who used racist language towards him. Four days later, 29-year-old Karl Anderson, a convicted football hooligan, pleaded guilty to racially aggravated common assault and was sentenced to 16 weeks in prison and a £100 fine.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Guardian</i> praised Sterling's resilience and courage in deciding to play only four hours afterwards.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, Sterling purchased a VVS gold name pendant for his two sons, Thai and Thiago. The jewelry which is estimated to cost $30,000, was designed by British-Nigerian designer and Jeweler, Godson Umeh.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sterling has an <a href="/wiki/M16_rifle" title="M16 rifle">M16 rifle</a> tattooed on his leg for which he received criticism from anti-violence groups, in response Sterling said that the tattoo had deeper meaning and referred to his father who was killed when Sterling was two years old.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> There has been criticism of how the British tabloid media, such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i>, cover and treat Sterling with articles being deemed unfair and racist by pundits including <a href="/wiki/Ian_Wright" title="Ian Wright">Ian Wright</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sterling has been named as one of the 100 most influential Black Britons, with his inclusion in the annual <i><a href="/wiki/Powerlist" title="Powerlist">Powerlist</a></i> in both the <a href="/wiki/Powerlist_2020" title="Powerlist 2020">2020</a> and <a href="/wiki/Powerlist_2021" title="Powerlist 2021">2021</a> editions.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 August 2020, Sterling attended a party to celebrate <a href="/wiki/Usain_Bolt" title="Usain Bolt">Usain Bolt</a>'s 34th birthday. The guests, who did not wear face masks, danced in an open field to Jamaican reggae singer <a href="/wiki/Koffee_(singer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Koffee (singer)">Koffee</a>'s song "Lockdown".<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Even before the confirmation that Bolt tested positive for <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019" class="mw-redirect" title="Coronavirus disease 2019">COVID-19</a> on 24 August and had to self-isolate in his home, Sterling was already advised to self-isolate as well after his possible exposure to the virus.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Sterling would be tested for the virus before he will be allowed into the training camp of the England national football team.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span></h2>
<p>In 2012, Sterling signed a sponsorship deal with American sportswear and equipment supplier, <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a>. He appeared in an advertisement for the new Nike Green Speed II alongside <a href="/wiki/Mario_G%C3%B6tze" title="Mario Götze">Mario Götze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theo_Walcott" title="Theo Walcott">Theo Walcott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eden_Hazard" title="Eden Hazard">Eden Hazard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Eriksen" title="Christian Eriksen">Christian Eriksen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stephan_El_Shaarawy" title="Stephan El Shaarawy">Stephan El Shaarawy</a> in November 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> In January 2013, he modelled the new <a href="/wiki/Nike_Mercurial_Vapor" title="Nike Mercurial Vapor">Nike Mercurial Vapor</a> IX.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
